IN\\n26:         const floating[:, ::1] centers,                # IN\\n27:         const floating[:, ::1] center_half_distances,  # IN\\n28:         int[::1] labels,                               # OUT\\n29:         floating[::1] upper_bounds,                    # OUT\\n30:         floating[:, ::1] lower_bounds,                 # OUT\\n31:         int n_threads):\\n32:     \\\"\\\"\\\"Initialize upper and lower bounds for each sample for dense input data.\\n33: \\n34:     Given X, centers and the pairwise distances divided by 2.0 between the\\n35:     centers this calculates the upper bounds and lower bounds for each sample.\\n36:     The upper bound for each sample is set to the distance between the sample\\n37:     and the closest center.\\n38: \\n39:     The lower bound for each sample is a one-dimensional array of n_clusters.\\n40:     For each sample i assume that the previously assigned cluster is c1 and the\\n41:     previous closest distance is dist, for a new cluster c2, the\\n42:     lower_bound[i][c2] is set to distance between the sample and this new\\n43:     cluster, if and only if dist > center_half_distances[c1][c2]. This prevents\\n44:     computation of unnecessary distances for each sample to the clusters that\\n45:     it is unlikely to be assigned to.\\n46: \\n47:     Parameters\\n48:     ----------\\n49:     X : ndarray of shape (n_samples, n_features), dtype=floating\\n50:         The input data.\\n51: \\n52:     centers : ndarray of shape (n_clusters, n_features), dtype=floating\\n53:         The cluster centers.\\n54: \\n55:     center_half_distances : ndarray of shape (n_clusters, n_clusters), \\\\\\n56:             dtype=floating\\n57:         The half of the distance between any 2 clusters centers.\\n58: \\n59:     labels : ndarray of shape(n_samples), dtype=int\\n60:         The label for each sample. This array is modified in place.\\n61: \\n62:     upper_bounds : ndarray of shape(n_samples,), dtype=floating\\n63:         The upper bound on the distance between each sample and its closest\\n64:         cluster center. This array is modified in place.\\n65: \\n66:     lower_bounds : ndarray, of shape(n_samples, n_clusters), dtype=floating\\n67:         The lower bound on the distance between each sample and each cluster\\n68:         center. This array is modified in place.\\n69: \\n70:     n_threads : int\\n71:         The number of threads to be used by openmp.\\n72:     \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n73:     cdef:\\n74:         int n_samples = X.shape[0]\\n75:         int n_clusters = centers.shape[0]\\n76:         int n_features = X.shape[1]\\n77: \\n78:         floating min_dist, dist\\n79:         int best_cluster, i, j\\n80: \\n81:     for i in prange(\\n82:         n_samples, num_threads=n_threads, schedule='static', nogil=True\\n83:     ):\\n84:         best_cluster = 0\\n85:         min_dist = _euclidean_dense_dense(&X[i, 0], &centers[0, 0],\\n86:                                           n_features, False)\\n87:         lower_bounds[i, 0] = min_dist\\n88:         for j in range(1, n_clusters):\\n89:             if min_dist > center_half_distances[best_cluster, j]:\\n90:                 dist = _euclidean_dense_dense(&X[i, 0], &centers[j, 0],\\n91:                                               n_features, False)\\n92:                 lower_bounds[i, j] = dist\\n93:                 if dist < min_dist:\\n94:                     min_dist = dist\\n95:                     best_cluster = j\\n96:         labels[i] = best_cluster\\n97:         upper_bounds[i] = min_dist\\n98: \\n99: \\n100: def init_bounds_sparse(\\n101:         X,                                             # IN\\n102:         const floating[:, ::1] centers,                # IN\\n103:         const floating[:, ::1] center_half_distances,  # IN\\n104:         int[::1] labels,                               # OUT\\n105:         floating[::1] upper_bounds,                    # OUT\\n106:         floating[:, ::1] lower_bounds,                 # OUT\\n107:         int n_threads):\\n108:     \\\"\\\"\\\"Initialize upper and lower bounds for each sample for sparse input data.\\n109: \\n110:     Given X, centers and the pairwise distances divided by 2.0 between the\\n111:     centers this calculates the upper bounds and lower bounds for each sample.\\n112:     The upper bound for each sample is set to the distance between the sample\\n113:     and the closest center.\\n114: \\n115:     The lower bound for each sample is a one-dimensional array of n_clusters.\\n116:     For each sample i assume that the previously assigned cluster is c1 and the\\n117:     previous closest distance is dist, for a new cluster c2, the\\n118:     lower_bound[i][c2] is set to distance between the sample and this new\\n119:     cluster, if and only if dist > center_half_distances[c1][c2]. OUT\\n30:         floating[:, ::1] lower_bounds,                 # OUT\\n31:         int n_threads):\\n32:     \\\"\\\"\\\"Initialize upper and lower bounds for each sample for dense input data.\\n33: \\n34:     Given X, centers and the pairwise distances divided by 2.0 between the\\n35:     centers this calculates the upper bounds and lower bounds for each sample.\\n36:     The upper bound for each sample is set to the distance between the sample\\n37:     and the closest center.\\n38: \\n39:     The lower bound for each sample is a one-dimensional array of n_clusters.\\n40:     For each sample i assume that the previously assigned cluster is c1 and the\\n41:     previous closest distance is dist, for a new cluster c2, the\\n42:     lower_bound[i][c2] is set to distance between the sample and this new\\n43:     cluster, if and only if dist > center_half_distances[c1][c2]. This prevents\\n44:     computation of unnecessary distances for each sample to the clusters that\\n45:     it is unlikely to be assigned to.\\n46: \\n47:     Parameters\\n48:     ----------\\n49:     X : ndarray of shape (n_samples, n_features), dtype=floating\\n50:         The input data.\\n51: \\n52:     centers : ndarray of shape (n_clusters, n_features), dtype=floating\\n53:         The cluster centers.\\n54: \\n55:     center_half_distances : ndarray of shape (n_clusters, n_clusters), \\\\\\n56:             dtype=floating\\n57:         The half of the distance between any 2 clusters centers.\\n58: \\n59:     labels : ndarray of shape(n_samples), dtype=int\\n60:         The label for each sample. This array is modified in place.\\n61: \\n62:     upper_bounds : ndarray of shape(n_samples,), dtype=floating\\n63:         The upper bound on the distance between each sample and its closest\\n64:         cluster center. This array is modified in place.\\n65: \\n66:     lower_bounds : ndarray, of shape(n_samples, n_clusters), dtype=floating\\n67:         The lower bound on the distance between each sample and each cluster\\n68:         center. These are the core functions that perform the distance calculations and label assignments.\n\nThe Elkan algorithm is designed to speed up K-means by using the triangle inequality to skip redundant distance calculations. The key insights are:\n\n1. **Upper bounds**: The distance from a sample to its current cluster is an upper bound on the distance to any other cluster.\n2. **Lower bounds**: The distance from a sample to a cluster is a lower bound.\n3. **Triangle inequality**: If the distance between two cluster centers is d, and we know the distance from a sample to center A is dist_A, then the distance from the sample to center B is at least |dist_A - d/2|.\n\nLooking at the current implementation in `_update_chunk_dense`:\n\nLines 377-421 show the main loop for processing each sample. OUT\n        floating[:, ::1] lower_bounds,                 # OUT\n        int n_threads):\n    \"\"\"Initialize upper and lower bounds for each sample for dense input data.\n\n    Given X, centers and the pairwise distances divided by 2.0 between the\n    centers this calculates the upper bounds and lower bounds for each sample.\n    The upper bound for each sample is set to the distance between the sample\n    and the closest center.\n\n    The lower bound for each sample is a one-dimensional array of n_clusters.\n    For each sample i assume that the previously assigned cluster is c1 and the\n    previous closest distance is dist, for a new cluster c2, the\n    lower_bound[i][c2] is set to distance between the sample and this new\n    cluster, if and only if dist > center_half_distances[c1][c2]. This prevents\n    computation of unnecessary distances for each sample to the clusters that\n    it is unlikely to be assigned to.\n\n    Parameters\n    ----------\n    X : ndarray of shape (n_samples, n_features), dtype=floating\n        The input data.\n\n    centers : ndarray of shape (n_clusters, n_features), dtype=floating\n        The cluster centers.\n\n    center_half_distances : ndarray of shape (n_clusters, n_clusters), \\\n            dtype=floating\n        The half of the distance between any 2 clusters centers.\n\n    labels : ndarray of shape(n_samples), dtype=int\n        The label for each sample. This array is modified in place.\n\n    upper_bounds : ndarray of shape(n_samples,), dtype=floating\n        The upper bound on the distance between each sample and its closest\n        cluster center.        - If True, the labels and the new centers will be computed, i.e. runs\n          the E-step and the M-step of the algorithm.\n        - If False, only the labels will be computed, i.e runs the This is useful especially when calling predict on a\n          fitted model.\n    \"\"\"\n    cdef:\n        int n_samples = X.shape[0]\n        int n_features = X.shape[1]\n        int n_clusters = centers_new.shape[0]\n\n    if n_samples == 0:\n        # An empty array was passed, do nothing and return early (before\n        # attempting to compute n_chunks). IN\n        int[::1] labels,                               # INOUT\n        floating[::1] upper_bounds,                    # INOUT\n        floating[:, ::1] lower_bounds,                 # INOUT\n        floating *centers_new,                         # OUT\n        floating *weight_in_clusters,                  # OUT\n        bint update_centers) noexcept nogil:\n    \"\"\"K-means combined EM step for one dense data chunk.\n\n    Compute the partial contribution of a single data chunk to the labels and\n    centers.\n    \"\"\"\n    cdef:\n        int n_samples = labels.shape[0]\n        int n_clusters = centers_old.shape[0]\n        int n_features = centers_old.shape[1]\n\n        floating upper_bound, distance\n        int i, j, k, label\n        int bounds_tight\n\n    for i in range(n_samples):\n        upper_bound = upper_bounds[i]\n        bounds_tight = 0\n        label = labels[i]\n\n        # Next center is not far away from the currently assigned center.\n        # Sample might need to be assigned to another center.\n        if not distance_next_center[label] >= upper_bound:\n\n            for j in range(n_clusters):\n\n                # If this holds, then center_index is a good candidate for the\n                # sample to be relabelled, and we need to confirm this by\n                # recomputing the upper and lower bounds.\n                if (\n                    j != label\n                    and (upper_bound > lower_bounds[i, j])\n                    and (upper_bound > center_half_distances[label, j])\n                ):\n\n                    # If the condition still holds, then compute the actual\n                    # distance between the sample and center. If this is less\n                    # than the previous distance, reassign label.\n                    if (\n                        upper_bound > lower_bounds[i, j]\n                        or (upper_bound > center_half_distances[label, j])\n                    ):\n\n                        distance = _euclidean_dense_dense(\n                            &X[i, 0], &centers_old[j, 0], n_features, False)\n                        lower_bounds[i, j] = distance\n                        if distance < upper_bound:\n                            label = j\n                            upper_bound = distance\n\n            labels[i] = label\n            upper_bounds[i] = upper_bound\n\n        if update_centers:\n            weight_in_clusters[label] += sample_weight[i]\n            for k in range(n_features):\n                centers_new[label * n_features + k] += X[i, k] * sample_weight[i]\n\n\ndef elkan_iter_chunked_sparse(\n        X,                                             # IN\n        const floating[::1] sample_weight,             # IN\n        const floating[:, ::1] centers_old,            # IN\n        floating[:, ::1] centers_new,                  # OUT\n        floating[::1] weight_in_clusters,              # OUT\n        const floating[:, ::1] center_half_distances,  # IN\n        const floating[::1] distance_next_center,      # IN\n        floating[::1] upper_bounds,                    # INOUT\n        floating[:, ::1] lower_bounds,                 # INOUT\n        int[::1] labels,                               # INOUT\n        floating[::1] center_shift,                    # OUT\n        int n_threads,\n        bint update_centers=True):\n    \"\"\"Single iteration of K-means Elkan algorithm with sparse input.\n\n    Update labels and centers (inplace), for one iteration, distributed\n    over data chunks.\n\n    Parameters\n    ----------\n    X : sparse matrix of shape (n_samples, n_features)\n        The observations to cluster. OUT\n        floating[:, ::1] lower_bounds,                 # OUT\n        int n_threads):\n    \"\"\"Initialize upper and lower bounds for each sample for dense input data.\n\n    Given X, centers and the pairwise distances divided by 2.0 between the\n    centers this calculates the upper bounds and lower bounds for each sample.\n    The upper bound for each sample is set to the distance between the sample\n    and the closest center.\n\n    The lower bound for each sample is a one-dimensional array of n_clusters.\n    For each sample i assume that the previously assigned cluster is c1 and the\n    previous closest distance is dist, for a new cluster c2, the\n    lower_bound[i][c2] is set to distance between the sample and this new\n    cluster, if and only if dist > center_half_distances[c1][c2]. This prevents\n    computation of unnecessary distances for each sample to the clusters that\n    it is unlikely to be assigned to.\n\n    Parameters\n    ----------\n    X : ndarray of shape (n_samples, n_features), dtype=floating\n        The input data.\n\n    centers : ndarray of shape (n_clusters, n_features), dtype=floating\n        The cluster centers.\n\n    center_half_distances : ndarray of shape (n_clusters, n_clusters), \\\n            dtype=floating\n        The half of the distance between any 2 clusters centers.\n\n    labels : ndarray of shape(n_samples), dtype=int\n        The label for each sample. This can typically happen when\n        # calling the prediction function of a bisecting k-means model with a\n        # large fraction of outliers.\n        return\n\n    cdef:\n        floating[::1] X_data = X.data\n        int[::1] X_indices = X.indices\n        int[::1] X_indptr = X.indptr\n\n        # hard-coded number of samples per chunk. Splitting in chunks is\n        # necessary to get parallelism. Chunk size chosen to be same as lloyd's\n        int n_samples_chunk = CHUNK_SIZE if n_samples > CHUNK_SIZE else n_samples\n        int n_chunks = n_samples // n_samples_chunk\n        int n_samples_rem = n_samples % n_samples_chunk\n        int chunk_idx\n        int start, end\n\n        int i, j, k\n\n        floating[::1] centers_squared_norms = row_norms(centers_old, squared=True)\n\n        floating *centers_new_chunk\n        floating *weight_in_clusters_chunk\n\n        omp_lock_t lock\n\n    # reduction from local buffers.\n        if update_centers:\n            # The lock is necessary to avoid race conditions when aggregating\n            # info from different thread-local buffers.\n            omp_set_lock(&lock)\n            for j in range(n_clusters):\n                weight_in_clusters[j] += weight_in_clusters_chunk[j]\n                for k in range(n_features):\n                    centers_new[j, k] += centers_new_chunk[j * n_features + k]\n            omp_unset_lock(&lock)\n\n        free(centers_new_chunk)\n        free(weight_in_clusters_chunk)\n\n    if update_centers:\n        omp_destroy_lock(&lock)\n        _relocate_empty_clusters_sparse(\n            X_data, X_indices, X_indptr, sample_weight,\n            centers_old, centers_new, weight_in_clusters, labels)\n\n        _average_centers(centers_new, weight_in_clusters)\n        _center_shift(centers_old, centers_new, center_shift)\n\n        # OUT\n        floating[:, ::1] lower_bounds,                 # OUT\n        int n_threads):\n    \"\"\"Initialize upper and lower bounds for each sample for dense input data.\n\n    Given X, centers and the pairwise distances divided by 2.0 between the\n    centers this calculates the upper bounds and lower bounds for each sample.\n    The upper bound for each sample is set to the distance between the sample\n    and the closest center.\n\n    The lower bound for each sample is a one-dimensional array of n_clusters.\n    For each sample i assume that the previously assigned cluster is c1 and the\n    previous closest distance is dist, for a new cluster c2, the\n    lower_bound[i][c2] is set to distance between the sample and this new\n    cluster, if and only if dist > center_half_distances[c1][c2]. This prevents\n    computation of unnecessary distances for each sample to the clusters that\n    it is unlikely to be assigned to.\n\n    Parameters\n    ----------\n    X : ndarray of shape (n_samples, n_features), dtype=floating\n        The input data.\n\n    centers : ndarray of shape (n_clusters, n_features), dtype=floating\n        The cluster centers.\n\n    center_half_distances : ndarray of shape (n_clusters, n_clusters), \\\n            dtype=floating\n        The half of the distance between any 2 clusters centers.\n\n    labels : ndarray of shape(n_samples), dtype=int\n        The label for each sample. This array is modified in place.\n\n    upper_bounds : ndarray of shape(n_samples,), dtype=floating\n        The upper bound on the distance between each sample and its closest\n        cluster center. This array is modified in place.\n\n    lower_bounds : ndarray, of shape(n_samples, n_clusters), dtype=floating\n        The lower bound on the distance between each sample and each cluster\n        center. This prevents\n    computation of unnecessary distances for each sample to the clusters that\n    it is unlikely to be assigned to.\n\n    Parameters\n    ----------\n    X : sparse matrix of shape (n_samples, n_features), dtype=floating\n        The input data. best_cluster = 0\n        min_dist = _euclidean_sparse_dense(\n            X_data[X_indptr[i]: X_indptr[i + 1]],\n            X_indices[X_indptr[i]: X_indptr[i + 1]],\n            centers[0], dist = _euclidean_sparse_dense(\n                    X_data[X_indptr[i]: X_indptr[i + 1]],\n                    X_indices[X_indptr[i]: X_indptr[i + 1]],\n                    centers[j],             # IN\n        const floating[:, ::1] centers_old,            # IN\n        floating[:, ::1] centers_new,                  # OUT\n        floating[::1] weight_in_clusters,              # OUT\n        const floating[:, ::1] center_half_distances,  # IN\n        const floating[::1] distance_next_center,      # IN\n        floating[::1] upper_bounds,                    # INOUT\n        floating[:, ::1] lower_bounds,                 # INOUT\n        int[::1] labels,                               # INOUT\n        floating[::1] center_shift,                    # OUT\n        int n_threads,\n        bint update_centers=True):\n    \"\"\"Single iteration of K-means Elkan algorithm with dense input.\n\n    Update labels and centers (inplace), for one iteration, distributed\n    over data chunks.\n\n    Parameters\n    ----------\n    X : ndarray of shape (n_samples, n_features), dtype=floating\n        The observations to cluster.\n\n    sample_weight : ndarray of shape (n_samples,), dtype=floating\n        The weights for each observation in X.\n\n    centers_old : ndarray of shape (n_clusters, n_features), dtype=floating\n        Centers before previous iteration, placeholder for the centers after\n        previous iteration.\n\n    centers_new : ndarray of shape (n_clusters, n_features), dtype=floating\n        Centers after previous iteration, placeholder for the new centers\n        computed during this iteration.\n\n    weight_in_clusters : ndarray of shape (n_clusters,), dtype=floating\n        Placeholder for the sums of the weights of every observation assigned\n        to each center.\n\n    center_half_distances : ndarray of shape (n_clusters, n_clusters), \\\n            dtype=floating\n        Half pairwise distances between centers.\n\n    distance_next_center : ndarray of shape (n_clusters,), dtype=floating\n        Distance between each center its closest center.\n\n    upper_bounds : ndarray of shape (n_samples,), dtype=floating\n        Upper bound for the distance between each sample and its center,\n        updated inplace.\n\n    lower_bounds : ndarray of shape (n_samples, n_clusters), dtype=floating\n        Lower bound for the distance between each sample and each center,\n        updated inplace.\n\n    labels : ndarray of shape (n_samples,), dtype=int\n        labels assignment.\n\n    center_shift : ndarray of shape (n_clusters,), dtype=floating\n        Distance between old and new centers.\n\n    n_threads : int\n        The number of threads to be used by openmp.\n\n    update_centers : bool\n        - If True, the labels and the new centers will be computed, i.e. runs\n          the E-step and the M-step of the algorithm.\n        - If False, only the labels will be computed, i.e runs the E-step of\n          the algorithm. This is useful especially when calling predict on a\n          fitted model.\n    \"\"\"\n    cdef:\n        int n_samples = X.shape[0]\n        int n_features = X.shape[1]\n        int n_clusters = centers_new.shape[0]\n\n    if n_samples == 0:\n        # An empty array was passed, do nothing and return early (before\n        # attempting to compute n_chunks). This can typically happen when\n        # calling the prediction function of a bisecting k-means model with a\n        # large fraction of outliers.\n        return\n\n    cdef:\n        # hard-coded number of samples per chunk. Splitting in chunks is\n        # necessary to get parallelism. Chunk size chosen to be same as lloyd's\n        int n_samples_chunk = CHUNK_SIZE if n_samples > CHUNK_SIZE else n_samples\n        int n_chunks = n_samples // n_samples_chunk\n        int n_samples_rem = n_samples % n_samples_chunk\n        int chunk_idx\n        int start, end\n\n        int i, j, k\n\n        floating *centers_new_chunk\n        floating *weight_in_clusters_chunk\n\n        omp_lock_t lock\n\n    # count remainder chunk in total number of chunks\n    n_chunks += n_samples != n_chunks * n_samples_chunk\n\n    # number of threads should not be bigger than number of chunks\n    n_threads = min(n_threads, n_chunks)\n\n    if update_centers:\n        memset(&centers_new[0, 0], 0, n_clusters * n_features * sizeof(floating))\n        memset(&weight_in_clusters[0], 0, n_clusters * sizeof(floating))\n        omp_init_lock(&lock)\n\n    with nogil, parallel(num_threads=n_threads):\n        # thread local buffers\n        centers_new_chunk = <floating*> calloc(n_clusters * n_features, sizeof(floating))\n        weight_in_clusters_chunk = <floating*> calloc(n_clusters, sizeof(floating))\n\n        for chunk_idx in prange(n_chunks, schedule='static'):\n            start = chunk_idx * n_samples_chunk\n            if chunk_idx == n_chunks - 1 and n_samples_rem > 0:\n                end = start + n_samples_rem\n            else:\n                end = start + n_samples_chunk\n\n            _update_chunk_dense(\n                X[start: end],\n                sample_weight[start: end],\n                centers_old,\n                center_half_distances,\n                distance_next_center,\n                labels[start: end],\n                upper_bounds[start: end],\n                lower_bounds[start: end],\n                centers_new_chunk,\n                weight_in_clusters_chunk,\n                update_centers)\n\n        # reduction from local buffers.\n        if update_centers:\n            # The lock is necessary to avoid race conditions when aggregating\n            # info from different thread-local buffers.\n            omp_set_lock(&lock)\n            for j in range(n_clusters):\n                weight_in_clusters[j] += weight_in_clusters_chunk[j]\n                for k in range(n_features):\n                    centers_new[j, k] += centers_new_chunk[j * n_features + k]\n            omp_unset_lock(&lock)\n\n        free(centers_new_chunk)\n        free(weight_in_clusters_chunk)\n\n    if update_centers:\n        omp_destroy_lock(&lock)\n        _relocate_empty_clusters_dense(X, sample_weight, centers_old,\n                                       centers_new, weight_in_clusters, labels)\n\n        _average_centers(centers_new, weight_in_clusters)\n        _center_shift(centers_old, centers_new, center_shift)\n\n        # update lower and upper bounds\n        for i in range(n_samples):\n            upper_bounds[i] += center_shift[labels[i]]\n\n            for j in range(n_clusters):\n                lower_bounds[i, j] -= center_shift[j]\n                if lower_bounds[i, j] < 0:\n                    lower_bounds[i, j] = 0\n\n\ncdef void _update_chunk_dense(\n        const floating[:, ::1] X,                      # IN\n        const floating[::1] sample_weight,             # IN\n        const floating[:, ::1] centers_old,            # IN\n        const floating[:, ::1] center_half_distances,  # IN\n        const floating[::1] distance_next_center,      # IN\n        int[::1] labels,                               # INOUT\n        floating[::1] upper_bounds,                    # INOUT\n        floating[:, ::1] lower_bounds,                 # INOUT\n        floating *centers_new,                         # OUT\n        floating *weight_in_clusters,                  # OUT\n        bint update_centers) noexcept nogil:\n    \"\"\"K-means combined EM step for one dense data chunk.\n\n    Compute the partial contribution of a single data chunk to the labels and\n    centers.\n    \"\"\"\n    cdef:\n        int n_samples = labels.shape[0]\n        int n_clusters = centers_old.shape[0]\n        int n_features = centers_old.shape[1]\n\n        floating upper_bound, distance\n        int i, j, k, label\n\n    for i in range(n_samples):\n        upper_bound = upper_bounds[i]\n        bounds_tight = 0\n        label = labels[i]\n\n        # Next center is not far away from the currently assigned center.\n        # Sample might need to be assigned to another center.\n        if not distance_next_center[label] >= upper_bound:\n\n            for j in range(n_clusters):\n\n                # If this holds, then center_index is a good candidate for the\n                # sample to be relabelled, and we need to confirm this by\n                # recomputing the upper and lower bounds.\n                if (\n                    j != label\n                    and (upper_bound > lower_bounds[i, j])\n                    and (upper_bound > center_half_distances[label, j])\n                ):\n\n                    # Recompute upper bound by calculating the actual distance\n                    # between the sample and its current assigned center.\n                    if not bounds_tight:\n                        upper_bound = _euclidean_dense_dense(\n                            &X[i, 0], &centers_old[label, 0], n_features, False)\n                        lower_bounds[i, label] = upper_bound\n                        bounds_tight = 1\n\n                    # If the condition still holds, then compute the actual\n                    # distance between the sample and center. If this is less\n                    # than the previous distance, reassign label.\n                    if (\n                        upper_bound > lower_bounds[i, j]\n                        or (upper_bound > center_half_distances[label, j])\n                    ):\n\n                        distance = _euclidean_dense_dense(\n                            &X[i, 0], &centers_old[j, 0], n_features, False)\n                        lower_bounds[i, j] = distance\n                        if distance < upper_bound:\n                            label = j\n                            upper_bound = distance\n\n            labels[i] = label\n            upper_bounds[i] = upper_bound\n\n        if update_centers:\n            weight_in_clusters[label] += sample_weight[i]\n            for k in range(n_features):\n                centers_new[label * n_features + k] += X[i, k] * sample_weight[i]\n\n\ndef elkan_iter_chunked_sparse(\n        X,                                             # IN\n        const floating[::1] sample_weight,             # IN\n        const floating[:, ::1] centers_old,            # IN\n        floating[:, ::1] centers_new,                  # OUT\n        floating[::1] weight_in_clusters,              # OUT\n        const floating[:, ::1] center_half_distances,  # IN\n        const floating[::1] distance_next_center,      # IN\n        floating[::1] upper_bounds,                    # INOUT\n        floating[:, ::1] lower_bounds,                 # INOUT\n        int[::1] labels,                               # INOUT\n        floating[::1] center_shift,                    # OUT\n        int n_threads,\n        bint update_centers=True):\n    \"\"\"Single iteration of K-means Elkan algorithm with sparse input.\n\n    Update labels and centers (inplace), for one iteration, distributed\n    over data chunks.\n\n    Parameters\n    ----------\n    X : sparse matrix of shape (n_samples, n_features)\n        The observations to cluster. Must be in CSR format.\n\n    sample_weight : ndarray of shape (n_samples,), dtype=floating\n        The weights for each observation in X.\n\n    centers_old : ndarray of shape (n_clusters, n_features), dtype=floating\n        Centers before previous iteration, placeholder for the centers after\n        previous iteration.\n\n    centers_new : ndarray of shape (n_clusters, n_features), dtype=floating\n        Centers after previous iteration, placeholder for the new centers\n        computed during this iteration.\n\n    weight_in_clusters : ndarray of shape (n_clusters,), dtype=floating\n        Placeholder for the sums of the weights of every observation assigned\n        to each center.\n\n    center_half_distances : ndarray of shape (n_clusters, n_clusters), \\\n            dtype=floating\n        Half pairwise distances between centers.\n\n    distance_next_center : ndarray of shape (n_clusters,), dtype=floating\n        Distance between each center its closest center.\n\n    upper_bounds : ndarray of shape (n_samples,), dtype=floating\n        Upper bound for the distance between each sample and its center,\n        updated inplace.\n\n    lower_bounds : ndarray of shape (n_samples, n_clusters), dtype=floating\n        Lower bound for the distance between each sample and each center,\n        updated inplace.\n\n    labels : ndarray of shape (n_samples,), dtype=int\n        labels assignment.\n\n    center_shift : ndarray of shape (n_clusters,), dtype=floating\n        Distance between old and new centers.\n\n    n_threads : int\n        The number of threads to be used by openmp.\n\n    update_centers : bool\n        - If True, the labels and the new centers will be computed, i.e. runs\n          the E-step and the M-step of the algorithm.\n        - If False, only the labels will be computed, i.e runs the E-step of\n          the algorithm. This is useful especially when calling predict on a\n          fitted model.\n    \"\"\"\n    cdef:\n        int n_samples = X.shape[0]\n        int n_features = X.shape[1]\n        int n_clusters = centers_new.shape[0]\n\n    if n_samples == 0:\n        # An empty array was passed, do nothing and return early (before\n        # attempting to compute n_chunks). This can typically happen when\n        # calling the prediction function of a bisecting k-means model with a\n        # large fraction of outliers.\n        return\n\n    cdef:\n        floating[::1] X_data = X.data\n        int[::1] X_indices = X.indices\n        int[::1] X_indptr = X.indptr\n\n        # hard-coded number of samples per chunk. Splitting in chunks is\n        # necessary to get parallelism. Chunk size chosen to be same as lloyd's\n        int n_samples_chunk = CHUNK_SIZE if n_samples > CHUNK_SIZE else n_samples\n        int n_chunks = n_samples // n_samples_chunk\n        int n_samples_rem = n_samples % n_samples_chunk\n        int chunk_idx\n        int start, end\n\n        int i, j, k\n\n        floating[::1] centers_squared_norms = row_norms(centers_old, squared=True)\n\n        floating *centers_new_chunk\n        floating *weight_in_clusters_chunk\n\n        omp_lock_t lock\n\n    # count remainder chunk in total number of chunks\n    n_chunks += n_samples != n_chunks * n_samples_chunk\n\n    # number of threads should not be bigger than number of chunks\n    n_threads = min(n_threads, n_chunks)\n\n    if update_centers:\n        memset(&centers_new[0, 0], 0, n_clusters * n_features * sizeof(floating))\n        memset(&weight_in_clusters[0], 0, n_clusters * sizeof(floating))\n        omp_init_lock(&lock)\n\n    with nogil, parallel(num_threads=n_threads):\n        # thread local buffers\n        centers_new_chunk = <floating*> calloc(n_clusters * n_features, sizeof(floating))\n        weight_in_clusters_chunk = <floating*> calloc(n_clusters, sizeof(floating))\n\n        for chunk_idx in prange(n_chunks, schedule='static'):\n            start = chunk_idx * n_samples_chunk\n            if chunk_idx == n_chunks - 1 and n_samples_rem > 0:\n                end = start + n_samples_rem\n            else:\n                end = start + n_samples_chunk\n\n            _update_chunk_sparse(\n                X_data[X_indptr[start]: X_indptr[end]],\n                X_indices[X_indptr[start]: X_indptr[end]],\n                X_indptr[start: end+1],\n                sample_weight[start: end],\n                centers_old,\n                centers_squared_norms,\n                center_half_distances,\n                distance_next_center,\n                labels[start: end],\n                upper_bounds[start: end],\n                lower_bounds[start: end],\n                centers_new_chunk,\n                weight_in_clusters_chunk,\n                update_centers)\n\n        # reduction from local buffers.\n        if update_centers:\n            # The lock is necessary to avoid race conditions when aggregating\n            # info from different thread-local buffers.\n            omp_set_lock(&lock)\n            for j in range(n_clusters):\n                weight_in_clusters[j] += weight_in_clusters_chunk[j]\n                for k in range(n_features):\n                    centers_new[j, k] += centers_new_chunk[j * n_features + k]\n            omp_unset_lock(&lock)\n\n        free(centers_new_chunk)\n        free(weight_in_clusters_chunk)\n\n    if update_centers:\n        omp_destroy_lock(&lock)\n        _relocate_empty_clusters_sparse(\n            X_data, X_indices, X_indptr, sample_weight,\n            centers_old, centers_new, weight_in_clusters, labels)\n\n        _average_centers(centers_new, weight_in_clusters)\n        _center_shift(centers_old, centers_new, center_shift)\n\n        # update lower and upper bounds\n        for i in range(n_samples):\n            upper_bounds[i] += center_shift[labels[i]]\n\n            for j in range(n_clusters):\n                lower_bounds[i, j] -= center_shift[j]\n                if lower_bounds[i, j] < 0:\n                    lower_bounds[i, j] = 0\n\n\ncdef void _update_chunk_sparse(\n        const floating[::1] X_data,                    # This meant it was treated as a Python object rather than a native type, incurring significant overhead for every access.\n\n**Solution Applied:**\nAdded proper Cython type declarations for `bounds_tight` as `cdef int bounds_tight` in both functions by moving it into the cdef variable declaration block.\n\n**Performance Impact:**\n- **Location**: Inner loops that process every sample in every cluster iteration\n- **Frequency**: Accessed once per sample per iteration in the main decision logic\n- **Speedup Mechanism**: \n  - Eliminates Python variable lookup overhead\n  - Reduces dynamic dispatch costs in tight loops\n  - For large datasets (thousands of samples × clusters), this compounds significantly\n\n### Patch Details\n\nThe patch makes two identical changes:\n1. **Line ~376** in `_update_chunk_dense()`: Added `int bounds_tight` declaration\n2. **Line ~633** in `_update_chunk_sparse()`: Added `int bounds_tight` declaration\n\nThis is a minimal, surgical change that targets the exact performance bottleneck without altering the algorithm's logic or correctness. The Elkan algorithm uses bounds (`bounds_tight` tracks whether we've computed the tight upper bound) to efficiently skip redundant distance calculations via triangle inequality.
